indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><msup><mi>R</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><msup><mi>T</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn><msup><mi>A</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><msup><mi>n</mi><mn>4</mn></msup><msup><mi>F</mi><mn>4</mn></msup><msup><mi>C</mi><mn>2</mn></msup><msup><mi>σ</mi><mn>2</mn></msup></mrow></mfrac></mstyle></mrow></math></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(7)</span></div></div><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq8"><div class="equation"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi>Z</mi><mi>re</mi></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi>R</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><msub><mi>R</mi><mi>ct</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mi>σ</mi><mo lspace="0.03em" rspace="0.03em">·</mo><msup><mi>ω</mi><mrow><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mo>/</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(8)</span></div></div><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq9"><div class="equation"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi>ω</mi></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mn>2</mn><mi>π</mi><mi>f</mi></mstyle></mrow></math></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(9)</span></div></div></div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Fitting Values of Resistance of Cube and Cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO Composites in LIBs</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">&nbsp;</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO cage</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO cube</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left"><i>R</i><sub>s</sub> (Ω)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">2.5</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">3.3</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left"><i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (Ω)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">160.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">250.8</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">The electrode interface was further analyzed by SEM and XPS as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>. SEM was used to study the morphology change of cage composite electrodes after cycling, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>a–f. It can be easily found that the interface engineering of the NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO nanocage makes the electrode thickness change little. In addition, the nanocage structure remains intact and there are no obvious cracks on the electrode surface. These results prove that hollow NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO nanocage can effectively inhibit the volume expansion during charge and discharge and enhance the cycle stability of the battery. The composition of the SEI film produced by the cycle was also explored by XPS in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 6</a>g–<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>i. When charging, the lithium ions undergo a detachment reaction. At the same time, the anions and solvent molecules in the electrolyte are adsorbed on the surface of the anode material accompanied by the reduction reaction, which generates inorganic components such as LiF, Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, and Li<sub>2</sub>O and organic components such as alkyl lithium. As the battery cycles further, the SEI film becomes denser and more stable, thus better preventing direct contact between the electrode and the electrolyte.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/medium/am4c06039_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/large/am4c06039_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Electrode cross section of cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO (a) before and (d) after 50 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>; the microstructure of cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO (b) before and (e) after 50 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>; the electrode surface morphology of cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO (c) before and (f) after 50 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>; and high-resolution XPS spectra of the SEI film including (g) C 1s; (h) O 1s; and (i) F 1s.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/large/am4c06039_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06039&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The rGO content had a significant influence on the conductivity of the electrode. To explore the effect of rGO addition on the electrode properties, the nanocage Ni–Co PBA@PDA and GO were synthesized with different proportions (1:0.5, 1:0.75, and 1:1), which are respectively denoted as NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-1, NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2, and NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-3. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5a</a> is the cycle performance comparison of different proportions of rGO. The cyclic curves of all three nanocage composites are relatively stable, indicating that coating rGO is conducive to improving the conductivity of the electrode, buffering the volume change, and showing higher theoretical specific capacity. Among them, NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 possesses a reversible capacity of 1392 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles and the capacity retention rate is 85.27%, which are much higher than those of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-1 (1060.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> and 74.06%) and NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-3 (1005.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> and 73.93%). The rate results of the three composites with different rGO contents are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S5b</a>. It is easily found that the specific capacity of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 is higher than that of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-1 and NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-3 at any current densities. When reverted to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 has a reversible capacity of 1231.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. It can be seen that the specific capacity of nanocage material with a mass ratio of 1:0.75 is still relatively stable, and there is no obvious descending trend. These indicate that NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 processes have the best rate performance. The long cycle properties of the three materials are compared at 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>. After 300 cycles, the NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 composite battery exhibits a satisfactory reversible capacity, which is up to 1126.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. In brief, the amount of rGO affects the battery performance. If the amount of rGO addition is too little, such as NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-1, the boost properties of the battery will be limited. But for NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-3, too much rGO leads to an increased electrode thickness and a stacked microstructure, which hinders the diffusion of Li<sup>+</sup> and weakens the cycle and rate performance. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> Moreover, the electrochemical properties of Ni–Co PBA, Ni–Co PBA@PDA, and NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 were also compared when they were used as anode active materials for LIBs, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>. When the current density is 1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the reversible capacity of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 is significantly higher than those of Ni–Co PBA and Ni–Co PBA@PDA. Therefore, etching treatment and reduced graphene oxide content are important for the comprehensive performance of LIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical properties of cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO and cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composites are explored in SIBs. The CV curve of the cage composite is shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>a. During the first cathode scan, there are three peaks corresponding to the reduction reactions. The peak at 0.96 V is related to electrochemical behavior of sodiation and the formation of the intermediate compound Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>M<sub>a</sub>S<sub>b</sub> (M = Ni, Co), which is depicted in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq10" aria-label="eq 10">eq 10</a>. Besides, there is a reduction peak located at 0.55 V, involving conversion of intermediate compounds to metal elements in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq11" aria-label="eq 11">eq 11</a>. Moreover, the peak at 0.69 V is related to the SEI formation. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51 ref52" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref51 ref52" aria-label="reference 51 and 52">(51,52)</a> In the subsequent cathode scanning, the peak at 0.55 V is split into two peaks at 0.46 and 0.83 V. And the reduction peak around 0.96 V moves to 1.42 V. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref53" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5 ref53" aria-label="reference 5 and 53">(5,53)</a> In addition, there are two spikes in the anode scan curve, corresponding to the reactions of the formation of NiS<sub>2</sub> (1.99 V) and Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (1.74 V) along with desodiation, which shift barely in subsequent scans. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref53" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21 ref53" aria-label="reference 21 and 53">(21,53)</a> The second and third CV curves display a high coincidence, which proves that the nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO has excellent reversibility. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>d, the CV curve of the cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite is shown, which presents similar trends and positions to the cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO, which manifests that ammonia etching hardly changes the storage mechanism of Na<sup>+</sup>. Moreover, the charge and discharge platforms of both cage and cube composites are consistent with the oxidation peaks and reduction peaks of CV tests as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>b,<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>e, which proves the reliability of the sodium storage mechanism in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq10" aria-label="eqs 10">eqs 10</a> and <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq11" aria-label="11">11</a>. Compared with the cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO, the open nanocage composite possesses higher specific capacity, and the capacity attenuation is less. The favorable performance is owing to that the open nanocage construction accelerates the sodiation and desodiation, improves reaction kinetics, and then enhances the electrochemical properties.<div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq10"><div class="equation"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi><mi>a</mi></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi><mi>b</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><msup><mrow><mi>x</mi><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mo>+</mo></msup><mo>+</mo><msup><mrow><mi>x</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi></mrow><mo>−</mo></msup></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">→</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi>Na</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi><mi>a</mi></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi><mi>b</mi></msub></mstyle></mrow></math></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(10)</span></div></div><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq11"><div class="equation"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mi>Na</mi><mi>x</mi></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">M</mi><mi>a</mi></msub><msub><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi><mi>b</mi></msub><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>b</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><msup><mi>Na</mi><mo>+</mo></msup><mo>+</mo><mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>2</mn><mi>b</mi><mo>−</mo><mi>x</mi><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="normal">e</mi><mo>−</mo></msup></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">→</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mi mathvariant="italic">aM</mi><mo>+</mo><msub><mrow><mi>b</mi><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mn>2</mn></msub><mi mathvariant="normal">S</mi></mstyle></mrow></math></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(11)</span></div></div></div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/medium/am4c06039_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/large/am4c06039_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. (a) CV curve and (b) charge and discharge curves of cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO; (c) GITT curve and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients at charge state; (d) CV curve and (e) charge and discharge curves of cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO; (f) GITT curve and Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients at discharge state; (g) EIS images and equivalent circuit diagrams of cube and cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO; (h) cycle performance (0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>); and (i) rate performance for the cube and cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composites comparison in SIBs.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/large/am4c06039_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06039&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>c,<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>f shows GITT curves of the cage and cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composites with a voltage range of 0–3 V and a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>. Sodium-ion diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i><sub>Na+</sub>) of the nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO is consistently larger during the charge and discharge state, which further manifests that the cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO provides more ion diffusion channels, shortens the diffusion path, and promotes the rapid diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>g was used to evaluate the electrochemical impedance of cube and cage composites. The equivalent circuit in the illustration was used to simulate the electrochemical impedance of cube and cage composites, which is shown in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl2" href="#tbl2">Table 2</a>. The <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of cage and cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composites are 519.1 and 828.9 Ω, respectively. The nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO demonstrates lower impedance, faster charge transfer rate, and better ion transport. Therefore, the comprehensive performance of the battery is validly improved using open NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO, which has excellent electrochemical dynamic performance, as an anode material.</div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl2"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 2. Fitting Values of Resistance of Cube and Cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO Composites in SIBs</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap" style="display: block;"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">&nbsp;</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO cage</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO cube</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left"><i>R</i><sub>s</sub> (Ω)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">5.6</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">11.5</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left"><i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (Ω)</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">519.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">828.9</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">To evaluate the cycle performance of cage and cube composites in SIBs, cycle tests are conducted, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>h. The initial charge and discharge capacities of this material are 1439.7 and 884.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, and the initial Coulombic efficiency is 61.4%. After 100 cycles, the open nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite exhibits a reversible capacity of 711.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with a capacity retention rate of 68.2%, which are much higher than those of the cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO (321.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, 60.2%). In addition, thanks to its rich pore structure and effective interface design, the open NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite shows better specific capacity and cycle performance than those in other studies, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 7</a>i, the rate test results are displayed to further analyze the sodium storage performance. The open nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO exhibits higher reversible capacities of 1031.2, 784.5, 714.7, 652.9, 584.6, and 487.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> from 0.1 to 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, while the nanocube composite exhibits capacities of only 548.9, 524, 452.7, 411.8, 340.7, and 239.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. After restoration to 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the specific capacity of nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO is 794.8 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. It is 376.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> higher than that of the cube NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite. Hence, the nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite has appreciable cycle and rate properties because of the open nanocage structure in SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p">To further study the storage mechanism of sodium ions, ex-suit XRD tests were carried out on electrode plates with different charge/discharge depths, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 8</a>. At the beginning, there are two diffraction peaks matching Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> and NiS<sub>2</sub> at 2θ = 31.9 and 33.4°, respectively. When the battery is discharged, the peak intensity of the two transition-metal sulfides gradually weakens and disappears until the discharge process is complete. At the same time, with the continuous insertion of sodium ions, the diffraction signal of Na<sub>2</sub>S (2θ = 39.1°) is enhanced. During charging, the diffraction peaks of Ni<sub>2</sub>S and Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> are increased, and the peak of Na<sub>2</sub>S gradually disappears. When fully charged, Na<sub>2</sub>S is converted to NiS<sub>2</sub> and Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, achieving the removal of sodium ions. These are consistent with the CV results, which proved that the redox reactions are reversible. It is well known that sodium-ion solvation has an important effect on the reversible. First, the surface properties of the electrode material affect the interaction between the solvated shell of the sodium ion and the electrode. In this study, the sodiation and desodiation behaviors were improved through strategies such as coating polydopamine and compounding with graphene oxide. In addition, the open NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite is structurally stable during sodium storage and avoids damage due to volume expansion and contraction, which is conducive to the rapid transport of sodium ions. In summary, the reversibility of sodiation and desodiation is achieved by adjusting sodium-ion solvation during sodium storage, thereby improving the electrical properties.</div><figure id="fig8" data-index="8" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 8</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/medium/am4c06039_0008.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/large/am4c06039_0008.jpeg" id="gr8" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 8. Ex situ XRD results of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO at different potentials.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/asset/images/large/am4c06039_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.4c06039&amp;id=fig8"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p last">The influences of different rGO contents on sodium storage properties are also investigated, as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>. At 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 has the best cycle performance with a specific capacity of 711.2 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, which is much higher than that of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-1 (480.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) and NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-3 (457.1 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>). <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.4c06039/suppl_file/am4c06039_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8b</a> displays the rate test results. When the current densities are 1, 2, and 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>, the reversible capacities of NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 can be up to 657.2, 579, and 475 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. These prove that the nanocage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO-2 has the best electrochemical properties with an rGO content of 0.75.</div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i23">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In this study, an NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO nanocage with an open structure was prepared by ammonia etching and two-step calcination, which is considered to be an outstanding anode material in both LIBs and SIBs. PBA-derived TMS provides abundant paths for the rapid transport of Li<sup>+</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> owing to the open nanocage structure. The conversion of transition metals between different oxidation states exhibits a considerable reversible capacity. The outstanding interface engineering of rGO and bimetallic sulfide improves the electrical conductivity, relieves volume stress, and reduces the agglomeration of the particles. Owing to these advantages, the reversible capacity of open NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO nanocage maintains 1392 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles, and the capacity retention rate is up to 85.2% in LIBs. Moreover, the cage NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO was also used in SIBs, which exhibits fantastic cycle and rate properties. It is worth noting that the reversible capacity of the open NiS<sub>2</sub>–Co<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO electrode is 249.9 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> higher than that of the cube (225.6 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>) at a current density of 5 A g<sup>–1</sup>. In conclusion, TMS and rGO have synergistic effect to boost the comprehensive performance of the batteries, and the combination of the two materials displays excellent development prospects for stored energy.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div                         cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Three-Dimensional Alkalized V2CTx MXene/NH2-Graphene Heterojunction Nanocomposites for Ammonia Detection at Room Temperature</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Jiangwei; Zhai, Haichao; Zhang, Ziwei; Di, Maoyun; Sun, Zhigang; Zhang, Kewei; Hu, Jifan; Fan, Huiqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Nano Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19797-19806</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AANMF6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2574-0970</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional MXene is considered a potential gas sensing material owing to its excellent cond., soln. processability, plentiful surface terminations, and alterable interlayer spacing.  Herein, we present the composites of the alkalized V2CTx MXene and NH2-graphene (NG) prepd. by simple sonication dispersion for ammonia (NH3) detection at room temp.  The alkalized V2CTx MXene was neg. charged, owing to the presence of abundant oxygen-contg. functional groups, which could interact with NG through electrostatic attraction.  The characterization results indicated that NG mainly connects to the surface of the alkalized V2CTx MXene nanosheets.  The gas response of the three-dimensional alkalized V2CTx MXene/NH2-graphene (AVNG) sensor was 21 times stronger than that of the alkalized V2CTx MXene.  Furthermore, the fabricated sensor based on the AVNG composites exhibited excellent selectivity to NH3, a moderate response/recovery time, good durability, and stability.  The gas sensing mechanism of the AVNG sensor was evaluated, and the synergistic effect of the interlayer swelling and n-p heterojunctions was proposed.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2023.144990"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, W.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, D.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In situ generated of hybrid interface in poly(1,3-dioxolane) quasi solid electrolyte and extended sulfone cosolvent for lithium-metal batteries</span>. <i>Chem. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2301308</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/advs.202301308</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DAdv.%2BSci.%26author%3DX.%2BX.%2BZhao%26author%3DW.%2BFu%26author%3DH.%2BX.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BZ.%2BGuo%26author%3DZ.%2BY.%2BGu%26author%3DX.%2BT.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BL.%2BYang%26author%3DH.%2BY.%2BL%25C3%25BC%26author%3DX.%2BL.%2BWu%26author%3DE.%2BH.%2BAng%26title%3DPearl-Structure-Enhanced%2BNASICON%2BCathode%2Btoward%2BUltrastable%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadvs.202301308&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06039&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadvs.202301308&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pearl-Structure-Enhanced NASICON Cathode toward Ultrastable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Xin-Xin; Fu, Wangqin; Zhang, Hong-Xia; Guo, Jin-Zhi; Gu, Zhen-Yi; Wang, Xiao-Tong; Yang, Jia-Lin; Lue, Hong-Yan; Wu, Xing-Long; Ang, Edison Huixiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Science (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2301308</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASDCCF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2198-3844</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Based on the favorable ionic cond. and structural stability, sodium superionic conductor (NASICON) materials esp. utilizing multivalent redox reaction of vanadium are one of the most promising cathodes in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  To further boost their application in large-scale energy storage prodn., a rational strategy is to tailor vanadium with earth-abundant and cheap elements (such as Fe, Mn), reducing the cost and toxicity of vanadium-based NASICON materials.  Here, the Na3.05V1.03Fe0.97(PO4)3 (NVFP) is synthesized with highly conductive Ketjen Black (KB) by ball-milling assisted sol-gel method.  The pearl-like KB branch chains encircle the NVFP (p-NVFP), the segregated particles possess promoted overall cond., balanced charge, and modulated crystal structure during electrochem. progress.  The p-NVFP obtains significantly enhanced ion diffusion ability and low vol. change (2.99%).  Meanwhile, it delivers a durable cycling performance (87.7% capacity retention over 5000 cycles at 5 C) in half cells.  Surprisingly, the full cells of p-NVFP reveal a remarkable capability of 84.9 mAh g-1 at 20 C with good cycling performance (capacity decay rate is 0.016% per cycle at 2 C).  The structure modulation of the p-NVFP provides a rational design on the superiority of others to be put into practice.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.scib.2023.08.038"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, Z.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Heng, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ang, E.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  A review discussing prospects and perspectives on advanced materials for sodium-ion batteries.  It as discusses parallel connections and integrates the two types of batteries in a certain manner and arrangement that ensures the balance of the different battery systems using the precise algorithms of battery management systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref7" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1007/s40843-022-2157-8"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Heng, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Geng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hollow Na<sub>0.62</sub>K<sub>0.05</sub>Mn<sub>0.7</sub>Ni<sub>0.2</sub>Co<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> polyhedra with exposed stable {001} facets and K riveting for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Sci. China Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>66</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">79</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">87</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1007/s40843-022-2157-8</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D66%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D79-87%26journal%3DSci.%2BChina%2BMater.%26author%3DZ.-X.%2BHuang%26author%3DX.-L.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.-X.%2BZhao%26author%3DY.-L.%2BHeng%26author%3DT.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BGeng%26author%3DX.-L.%2BWu%26title%3DHollow%2BNa0.62K0.05Mn0.7Ni0.2Co0.1O2%2Bpolyhedra%2Bwith%2Bexposed%2Bstable%2B%257B001%257D%2Bfacets%2Band%2BK%2Briveting%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1007%252Fs40843-022-2157-8&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06039&amp;doiOfLink=10.1007%2Fs40843-022-2157-8&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hollow Na0.62K0.05Mn0.7Ni0.2Co0.1O2 polyhedra with exposed stable {001} facets and K riveting for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Zhi-Xiong; Zhang, Xue-Li; Zhao, Xin-Xin; Heng, Yong-Li; Wang, Ting; Geng, Hongbo; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science China Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">66</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">79-87</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCMCDB</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-8226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science China Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, there has been an increased interest in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), in which cathodes that directly det. the performance of batteries play a crit. role.  Among the cathode materials, layered oxide cathodes are the most fascinating electrode materials for SIBs.  However, irreversible phase transition, low capacity, poor air stability, and inferior cycling stability limit the application of layered oxides.  In this study, hollow P2-Na0.62K0.05Mn0.7Ni0.2Co0.1O2 polyhedra consisting of nanosheets with exposed stable {001} facets and a small amt. of large-size K+ ions partly replacing Na+ ions were successfully obtained.  By virtue of the high redox potential of Ni2+/4+, it can be stored in air for several days.  It also exhibits a high discharge capacity of 115.0 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  A preeminent discharge capacity of 104.1 mA h g-1 can be achieved even at 500 mA g-1.  Results showed that such performances are related to the block of phase transition from P2 to O2 and to the riveting of K+ ions, which expands the interlayer space (d(O-Na-O)) and accelerates the transfer of sodium.  Thus, the P2-Na0.62K0.05Mn0.7Ni0.2Co0.1O2 cathode is one of the promising cathode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref8" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.3390/nano14010118"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kou, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-situ construction of anti-aggregation tellurium nanorods/reduced graphene oxide composite to enable fast sodium storage</span>. <i>Nanomaterials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">118</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-organic framework-derived transition metal sulfides and their composites for alkali-ion batteries: A review</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Jian-En; Chen, Jiahao; Peng, Yanhua; Zheng, Yongqian; Zeb, Akif; Lin, Xiaoming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Coordination Chemistry Reviews</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Transition metal sulfides (TMSs) have been regarded as promising anodes for alkali-ion batteries with high energy densities.  They possess higher ionic/electronic conductivities as compared to their counterparts such as transition metal oxides and phosphides.  However, their large volumetric expansion and bulk properties lead to slow ion transport and severe capacity attenuation, esp. during the alloying and conversion reactions.  Furthermore, to design better electrode materials, it is necessary to develop a clear understanding of their kinetic properties and reaction mechanisms in alkali-ion batteries (AIBs).  As a new class of materials that have shown revolutionary progress in various catalytic and electrochem. processes in environmental and energy storage and conversion applications, metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) have recently attracted significant attention as an effective soln. to these problems.  Herein, we discuss the strategies developed to mitigate these problems with the help of MOF-derived TMS-based electrode materials, the mechanisms involved and the advantages, challenges, and prospects in their application as anode/cathode materials in AIBs including lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), and potassium-ion batteries (PIBs).  We hope that this review will guide further research and facilitate the practical application of MOF-derived TMS-based materials for sulfide-based high-performance rechargeable AIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2022.136080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bian, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Heterostructured WS<sub>2</sub>/MoS<sub>2</sub>@carbon hollow microspheres anchored on graphene for high-performance Li/Na storage</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">With the increasing popularity of new energy elec. vehicles, the demand for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) has been growing rapidly, which will produce a large no. of spent LIBs.  Therefore, recycling of spent LIBs has become an urgent task to be solved, otherwise it will inevitably lead to serious environmental pollution.  Herein, a unique recycling strategy is proposed to achieve the concurrent reuse of cathode and anode in the spent graphite/LiFePO4 batteries.  Along with such recycling process, a unique cathode composed of recycled LFP/graphite (RLFPG) with cation/anion-co-storage ability is designed for new-type dual-ion battery (DIB).  As a result, the recycle-derived DIB of Li/RLFPG is established with good electrochem. performance, such as an initial discharge capacity of 117.4 mA h g-1 at 25 mA g-1 and 78% capacity retention after 1000 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  The working mechanism of Li/RLFPG DIB is also revealed via in situ X-ray diffraction and electrode kinetics studies.  This work not only presents a far-reaching significance for large-scale recycling of spent LIBs in the future, but also proposed a sustainable and economical method to design new-type secondary batteries as recycling of spent LIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref20" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1007/s41918-021-00114-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effects of crystallinity and defects of layered carbon materials on potassium storage: A review and prediction</span>. <i>Electrochem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Novel Ni-Co Prussian Blue nanocage (PBA) analogs consisting of pyramid-like walls by treating Ni-Co PBA cubes with ammonia at room temp.  The precursor cubes undergo a very unusual structural evolution and transform into a cage-like nanostructure, which is likely due to the inhomogeneous surface reactivity of the cubes.  The Ni-Co PBA cages can be further transformed into Ni-Co mixed oxide cages by calcination in air.  The resulting Ni-Co mixed oxide cages exhibit enhanced OER (oxygen evolution reaction) activity with a small overpotential of 0.38 V at the c.d. of 10 mA.cm-2, and good durability in alk. medium.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2020.227737"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.-E.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Growing NiS<sub>2</sub> nanosheets on porous carbon microtubes for hybrid sodium-ion capacitors</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jpowsour.2020.227737</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D451%26publication_year%3D2020%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DJ.%2BZhao%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26author%3DK.%2BCheng%26author%3DK.%2BYe%26author%3DK.%2BZhu%26author%3DJ.%2BYan%26author%3DD.%2BCao%26author%3DH.-E.%2BWang%26title%3DGrowing%2BNiS2%2Bnanosheets%2Bon%2Bporous%2Bcarbon%2Bmicrotubes%2Bfor%2Bhybrid%2Bsodium-ion%2Bcapacitors%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2020.227737&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06039&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2020.227737&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Growing NiS2 nanosheets on porous carbon microtubes for hybrid sodium-ion capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Jing; Wang, Guiling; Cheng, Kui; Ye, Ke; Zhu, Kai; Yan, Jun; Cao, Dianxue; Wang, Hong-En</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">451</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">227737</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">NiS2 is a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and capacitors (SICs).  However, the sluggish Na+ diffusion and large vol. change of bulk NiS2 during sodiation/de-sodiation lead to poor rate capability and fast capacity decay, limiting its practical application.  Herein, well-oriented NiS2 nanosheets are designed and prepd. on porous carbon microtubes (denoted as NiS2/pCMT) as a novel anode material for SIBs/SHCs.  The unique porous hollow carbon tubes and NiS2 nanosheets can well relieve the repeated stress/strain and maintain the structural integrity of the composite anode during long-term charging/discharging.  As a confirmation, a modeled SHC is constructed by using the NiS2/pCMT composite as anode and coupling with an activated carbon cathode, delivering a high energy d. of 136 Wh kg-1 and good cycling stability.  The first-principles d. functional theory (DFT) calcns. confirm that the NiS2 nanosheets surface has a high chem. affinity towards Na+ ions, promising the concn. of Na+ ion on/nearby the surface for fast redox reactions during sodiation/de-sodiation of NiS2.  This work provides some new insights for the design and fabrication novel composite electrode materials for applications in beyond lithium-ion batteries/capacitors.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1039/D3QI00019B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ruan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.-R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mei, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dendritic NiS<sub>2</sub>@Co–N–C nanoarchitectures as bifunctional electrocatalysts for long-life Zn–air batteries</span>. <i>Inorg.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ-Formed Hollow Cobalt Sulfide Wrapped by Reduced Graphene Oxide as an Anode for High-Performance Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Shi-jie; Wang, Zhi-teng; Zhang, Xia-hui; He, Zhen-jiang; Tong, Hui; Li, Yun-jiao; Zheng, Jun-chao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2671-2678</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition-metal sulfides have been considered as promising anode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their high theor. specific capacity and superior electrochem. performance.  However, the large vol. change during the discharge/charge process causes structural pulverization, resulting in rapid capacity decline and the loss of active materials.  Herein, we report Co1-xS hollow spheres formed by in situ growth on reduced graphene oxide layers.  When evaluated as an anode material for LIBs, it delivers a specific capacity of 969.8 mAh·g-1 with a high Coulombic efficiency of 96.49% after 90 cycles.  Furthermore, a high reversible capacity of 527.2 mAh·g-1 after the 107th cycle at a c.d. of 2.5 A g-1 is still achieved.  The results illustrate that in situ growth on the graphene layers can enhance cond. and restrain vol. expansion of cobalt sulfide compared with ex situ growth.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2020.04.024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">You, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Won, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yun, Y.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-patching defects of reduced graphene oxide by cellulose nanocrystals in scalable polymer nanocomposites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">You, Jinhwa; Won, Sukyoung; Jin, Hyoung-Joon; Yun, Young Soo; Wie, Jeong Jae</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">165</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18-25</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Reduced graphene oxide (rGO) has been widely produced by exfoliation of pristine graphite followed by oxidn. and redn.  However, a no. of defects can be generated during the synthesis of rGO, restricting the ability to scale-up in industrial prodn. of defect-free rGO.  The defects in rGO have limited its capacity for utilization of the full potential of the phys. properties of polymer nanocomposites, such as gas and water barrier performances.  Hence, this study analyzes the nano-patching of rGO defects through hydrophilic interactions of oxygen functional groups in rGO with cellulose nanocrystals (CNCs) in polyvinylidene chloride (PVDC) nanocomposites.  For scalable prodn. of defect-engineered PVDC nanocomposite barrier films, the surface energies of rGO and CNC dual nanofiller systems were regulated to prevent phase-sepn. of nanofillers in the PVDC matrixes.  The barrier properties of the PVDC/nano-patched filler composites showed drastic redn. of oxygen and water vapor transmission rates corresponding to 0.45 cm3 m-2 day-1 and 0.52 cm3 m-2 day-1, resp., that decreased by 94.2% and 87.9% compared to that of the neat PVDC host.  The nano-patching strategy provides novel and effective defect engineering of graphene for polymer nanocomposites.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref31" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1007/s11431-022-2226-8"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Biomass-derived self-supporting sulfur host with NiS/C composite for high-loading Li-S battery cathode</span>. <i>Sci.                 10.1016/j.electacta.2023.142705</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D462%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DJ.%2BCai%26author%3DX.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BDuan%26author%3DG.%2BYang%26author%3DQ.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BFan%26author%3DZ.%2BLiu%26author%3DF.%2BPeng%26title%3DPorous%2BNiS2%2Bnanosheets%2Banchored%2Bon%2Breduced%2Bgraphene%2Boxide%2Bas%2Bhigh-rate%2Band%2Blong-life%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2023.142705&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06039&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2023.142705&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous NiS2 nanosheets anchored on reduced graphene oxide as high-rate and long-life anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cai, Jianzhong; Chen, Xunjie; Duan, Xuezhi; Yang, Guangxing; Zhang, Qiao; Fan, Haosen; Liu, Zhiting; Peng, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">462</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">142705</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, graphene oxide is used as a substrate for the nucleation and growth of Ni(OH)(OCH3) during solvothermal synthesis.  As a result, 2D Ni(OH)(OCH3) nanosheets are vertically anchored on 2D reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanosheets, forming a Ni(OH)(OCH3)@rGO composite.  Afterward, a NiS2@rGO hybrid is created by sulfurizing the Ni(OH)(OCH3)@rGO intermediate, which presents the same morphol. as the intermediate but a porous structure of NiS2 nanosheets.  The characteristic 2D porous structure of NiS2 nanosheets offers abundant active sites for charge storage, accelerates ion/electron transport, and buffers vol. expansion.  Meanwhile, rGO nanosheets can suppress the shuttle of polysulfides while also enhancing elec. cond.  These factors in conjunction with the thin and robust ether-derived SEI are favorable to mech. stability and rapid sodiation kinetics in the NiS2@rGO electrode in the ether-based electrolyte, thereby endowing it with exceptional rate capability (324 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1) and a long lifespan (378 mA h g-1 over 1800 cycles at 1 A g-1).  However, in the ester-based electrolyte, NiS2@rGO shows poor rate capability and cyclability.  The kinetic anal. unveils the mechanism underlying the different electrochem. behavior in NiS2@rGO in the two electrolytes.  More importantly, the NiS2@rGO electrode outperforms most NiS2-based materials reported in terms of rate and cycling performance owing to its unique hierarchical structure, making it a viable contender for anode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  We also propose a novel M(OH)(OCH3)@rGO intermediate for the fabrication of transition-metal oxides/sulfides@rGO composites for energy storage and catalysis.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2023.141713"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cong, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In situ N-doped carbon nanotubes modified NiS<sub>2</sub> hierarchical hollow microspheres for boosting sodium storage performance</span>. <i>Chem.                         "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202202388"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Solvated sodium storage via a coadsorptive mechanism in microcrystalline graphite fiber</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">2202388</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202202388</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DT.%2BWang%26author%3DT.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BSun%26author%3DT.%2BJi%26author%3DJ.%2BTian%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BHao%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DD.%2BChao%26title%3DSolvated%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%2Bvia%2Ba%2Bcoadsorptive%2Bmechanism%2Bin%2Bmicrocrystalline%2Bgraphite%2Bfiber%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202202388&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06039&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202202388&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Solvated Sodium Storage via a Coadsorptive Mechanism in Microcrystalline Graphite Fiber</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xiaoxu; Wang, Tian; Zhang, Tengsheng; Sun, Zhihao; Ji, Tianyi; Tian, Jing; Wang, Hui; Hao, Xiaodong; Liu, Hui; Chao, Dongliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2202388</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite has been widely accepted for its reversible solvated sodium cointercalation mechanism into the graphite layers in ether-based electrolytes.  However, the cointercalation suffers from insufficient Coulombic efficiency with high redox potentials, which significantly limits its energy output.  Herein, instead of the conventional solvated Na+ cointercalation into the graphite, a new coadsorptive mechanism is proposed through the microcryst. graphite fiber (MCGF), which can reversibly store the solvated Na+ at the ribboned grain boundaries and in the mesopores of the MCGF.  The mechanism is manifested by various advanced spectroscopy techniques, including in situ synchrotron small-angle X-ray scattering to track the long-periodic structure evolution and ex situ synchrotron X-ray absorption fine structure to verify the interaction of solvated Na and graphite layers.  The origin of the boosted rate-capability and reversibility is further revealed by d. functional theory simulations and aberration-cor. transmission electron microscopy.  As a proof-of-concept, the MCGF electrode exhibits high initial coulombic efficiency (92.5%), fast-charging (within 4 min), and enhanced cycling stability (≈98% retention after 800 cycles).  The results provide a new understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in graphite-based materials, which may inspire further exploration of carbon electrodes for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.cclet.2023.108471"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Inspired by nature: Self-fractal cobalt sulfate composite electrode for sodium ion storage</span>. <i>Chin. Chem. Lett.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>34</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">108471</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.cclet.2023.108471</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D34%26publication_year%3D2023%26journal%3DChin.%2BChem.%2BLett.%26author%3DM.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BGu%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DZ.%2BShen%26title%3DInspired%2Bby%2Bnature%253A%2BSelf-fractal%2Bcobalt%2Bsulfate%2Bcomposite%2Belectrode%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cclet.2023.108471&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c06039&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cclet.2023.108471&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Inspired by nature: Self-fractal cobalt sulfate composite electrode for sodium ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Man; Liu, Xiaoxu; Gu, Jiangdong; Wang, Hui; Liu, Hui; Shen, Zexiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chinese Chemical Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">108471</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CCLEE7</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1001-8417</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generally, the metal sulfide itself has poor cond., and the vol. expansion occurs when it is converted with sodium, which will destroy the integrity of the electrode structure, resulting in poor cycle performance and rate performance.  To solve the problems of low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) and vol. expansion of metal compds. used as anodes in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Inspired by nature, the CoSO4/hard carbon/graphene (CHG) fractal structure electrode was designed.  Self-fractal structures with electron/ion transport channels and high strain tolerance proved to be an effective strategy to overcome these challenges.  The fractal dimension (D) is measured by synchronous Small Angle X-ray scattering, and the D remains stable during charging and discharging.  The fractal CHG also showed excellent electrochem. performance, esp. 97.4% ICE.  Theor. calcn. shows that self-fractal CHG can promote the formation of a thin solid electrolyte interface (SEI).  Synchrotron radiation absorption spectrum proved the reaction mechanism of CHG.  This study not only proves that cobalt sulfate is a feasible strategy for developing high-performance SIBs anodes but also provides an advanced method for measuring the fractal dimension of energy storage electrode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.2c17568"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Controlling of Ni-Based Composites in Salt Melt Synthesis with High Sodium-Ion Storage Performance</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NiCo2S4 Nanosheets Grown on 3D Networks of Nitrogen-Doped Graphene/Carbon Nanotubes: Advanced Anode Materials for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Longsheng; Zuo, Lizeng; Fan, Wei; Liu, Tianxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To meet the requirements of high-performance lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), a new class of electrode materials with favorable nanostructures is highly desirable.  Recently, metal sulfides have been intensively studied as promising anode materials for LIBs because of their high lithium storage capacity.  Among them, ternary metal sulfides can provide much higher electrochem. activity and energy storage performance than binary metal sulfides or their oxide counterparts, which makes them outstanding candidates as anode materials for next-generation LIBs.  In this work, hierarchical nanostructured hybrids of NiCo2S4 nanosheets uniformly grown on nitrogen-doped graphene/carbon nanotube networks (NiCo2S4/NGC) have been easily prepd. as novel anode materials for LIBs.  Benefiting from the synergistic effects between NiCo2S4 nanosheets and conductive NGC networks, the optimized NiCo2S4/NGC hybrid exhibits greatly enhanced electrochem. performance with high initial charge capacity of 1225.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 and excellent cycling stability with 89 % capacity retention after 100 cycles. Bimetallic sulfide composites are one of the emerging catalysts for hydrogen evolution reactions (HER) during water splitting.  Herein, a hydrothermal method has been employed for the in-situ synthesis of NiS2 nanoparticles/MoS2 nanosheets (NiS2/MoS2) hierarchical sphere anchored on reduced graphene oxide (RGO) for enhanced electrocatalytic HER activity.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extra storage capacity in transition metal oxide lithium-ion batteries revealed by in situ magnetometry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Qiang; Li, Hongsen; Xia, Qingtao; Hu, Zhengqiang; Zhu, Yue; Yan, Shishen; Ge, Chen; Zhang, Qinghua; Wang, Xiaoxiong; Shang, Xiantao; Fan, Shuting; Long, Yunze; Gu, Lin; Miao, Guo-Xing; Yu, Guihua; Moodera, Jagadeesh S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">76-83</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NMAACR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1476-1122</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Research</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), many promising electrodes that are based on transition metal oxides exhibit anomalously high storage capacities beyond their theor. values.  Although this phenomenon has been widely reported, the underlying physicochem. mechanism in such materials remains elusive and is still a matter of debate.  In this work, we use in situ magnetometry to demonstrate the existence of strong surface capacitance on metal nanoparticles, and to show that a large no. of spin-polarized electrons can be stored in the already-reduced metallic nanoparticles (that are formed during discharge at low potentials in transition metal oxide LIBs), which is consistent with a space charge mechanism.  Through quantification of the surface capacitance by the variation in magnetism, we further show that this charge capacity of the surface is the dominant source of the extra capacity in the Fe3O4/Li model system, and that it also exists in CoO, NiO, FeF2 and Fe2N systems.  The space charge mechanism revealed by in situ magnetometry can therefore be generalized to a broad range of transition metal compds. for which a large electron d. of states is accessible, and provides pivotal guidance for creating advanced energy storage systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1039/D3TA04794F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hashem, A.                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Understanding Excess Li Storage beyond LiC6 in Reduced Dimensional Scale Graphene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Dong Won; Jung, Sung Mi; Senthil, Chenrayan; Kim, Sun-Sik; Ju, Byeong-Kwon; Jung, Hyun Young</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">797-808</span>CODEN:
